     <p>
      The
      <b>
       coconut tree
      </b>
      (
      <i>
       <b>
        Cocos nucifera
       </b>
      </i>
      ) is a member of the
      <a href="/wiki/Family_(biology)" title="Family (biology)">
       family
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Arecaceae" title="Arecaceae">
       Arecaceae
      </a>
      (palm family).
     </p>
     <p>
      It is the only accepted species in the
      <a href="/wiki/Genus" title="Genus">
       genus
      </a>
      <i>
       <b>
        Cocos
       </b>
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The term
      <b>
       coconut
      </b>
      can refer to the entire
      <b>
       coconut palm
      </b>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Seed" title="Seed">
       seed
      </a>
      , or the
      <a href="/wiki/Fruit" title="Fruit">
       fruit
      </a>
      , which, botanically, is a
      <a href="/wiki/Drupe" title="Drupe">
       drupe
      </a>
      , not a
      <a href="/wiki/Nut_(fruit)" title="Nut (fruit)">
       nut
      </a>
      . The spelling
      <b>
       cocoanut
      </b>
      is an archaic form of the word.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-COD_3-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-COD-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The term is derived from the 16th-century Portuguese and Spanish word
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Coco_(folklore)" title="Coco (folklore)">
        coco
       </a>
      </i>
      meaning "head" or "skull", from the three indentations on the coconut shell that resemble facial features.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The coconut is known for its great versatility as seen in the many uses of its different parts and found throughout the tropics and subtropics.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Coconuts are part of the daily diets of many people. Coconuts are different from any other fruits because they contain a large quantity of "water" and when immature they are known as tender-nuts or jelly-nuts and may be harvested for drinking. When mature, they still contain some water and can be used as seednuts or processed to give oil from the kernel,
      <a href="/wiki/Charcoal" title="Charcoal">
       charcoal
      </a>
      from the hard shell and
      <a href="/wiki/Coir" title="Coir">
       coir
      </a>
      from the fibrous husk. The
      <a href="/wiki/Endosperm" title="Endosperm">
       endosperm
      </a>
      is initially in its nuclear phase suspended within the coconut water. As development continues, cellular layers of endosperm deposit along the walls of the coconut, becoming the edible coconut "flesh".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-endosperm_6-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-endosperm-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      When dried, the coconut flesh is called
      <a href="/wiki/Copra" title="Copra">
       copra
      </a>
      . The
      <a href="/wiki/Coconut_oil" title="Coconut oil">
       oil
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Coconut_milk" title="Coconut milk">
       milk
      </a>
      derived from it are commonly used in cooking and frying; coconut oil is also widely used in
      <a href="/wiki/Soap" title="Soap">
       soaps
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Cosmetics" title="Cosmetics">
       cosmetics
      </a>
      . The clear liquid
      <a href="/wiki/Coconut_water" title="Coconut water">
       coconut water
      </a>
      within is potable. The husks and leaves can be used as material to make a variety of products for furnishing and decorating. It also has cultural and religious significance in many societies that use it.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2014)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="toclimit-2">

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Description">
       Description
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Coconut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Description">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Coconut_Palm_flowers.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="1067" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Coconut_Palm_flowers.jpg/170px-Coconut_Palm_flowers.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Coconut_Palm_flowers.jpg/255px-Coconut_Palm_flowers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Coconut_Palm_flowers.jpg/340px-Coconut_Palm_flowers.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Coconut_Palm_flowers.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Coconut flowers
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Plant">
       Plant
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Coconut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Plant">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <i>
       Cocos nucifera
      </i>
      is a large palm, growing up to 30m (98ft) tall, with
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pinnate" title="Pinnate">
       pinnate
      </a>
      leaves 46m (1320ft) long, and pinnae 6090cm long; old leaves break away cleanly, leaving the
      <a href="/wiki/Trunk_(botany)" title="Trunk (botany)">
       trunk
      </a>
      smooth. Coconuts are generally classified into two general types: tall and dwarf.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pradeepkumar_7-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Pradeepkumar-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On very fertile land, a tall coconut palm tree can yield up to 75 fruits per year, but more often yields less than 30, mainly due to poor cultural practices.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Grimwood18_8-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Grimwood18-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sarian_9-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Sarian-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ravi_10-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Ravi-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Given proper care and growing conditions coconut palms produce their first fruit in six to ten years, it takes 15  20 years to reach peak production.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
       <a href="#cite_note-11">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        11
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Fruit">
       Fruit
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Coconut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Fruit">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Botany" title="Botany">
       Botanically
      </a>
      , the coconut
      <a href="/wiki/Fruit" title="Fruit">
       fruit
      </a>
      is a
      <a href="/wiki/Drupe" title="Drupe">
       drupe
      </a>
      , not a true
      <a href="/wiki/Nut_(fruit)" title="Nut (fruit)">
       nut
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
       <a href="#cite_note-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Like other fruits, it has
      <a href="/wiki/Fruit_anatomy" title="Fruit anatomy">
       three layers
      </a>
      : the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exocarp" title="Exocarp">
       exocarp
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mesocarp" title="Mesocarp">
       mesocarp
      </a>
      , and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Endocarp" title="Endocarp">
       endocarp
      </a>
      . The exocarp and mesocarp make up the "husk" of the coconut. Coconuts sold in the shops of nontropical countries often have had the exocarp (outermost layer) removed. The mesocarp is composed of a
      <a href="/wiki/Fiber" title="Fiber">
       fiber
      </a>
      , called
      <a href="/wiki/Coir" title="Coir">
       coir
      </a>
      , which has many traditional and commercial uses. The shell has three
      <a href="/wiki/Germination" title="Germination">
       germination
      </a>
      pores (
      <a href="/wiki/Stoma" title="Stoma">
       stoma
      </a>
      ) or "eyes" that are clearly visible on its outside surface once the husk is removed.
     </p>
     <p>
      A full-sized coconut weighs about 1.44kg (3.2lb). It takes around 6,000 full-grown coconuts to produce a tonne of
      <a href="/wiki/Copra" title="Copra">
       copra
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
       <a href="#cite_note-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Roots">
       Roots
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Coconut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Roots">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Unlike some other plants, the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palm_tree" title="Palm tree">
       palm tree
      </a>
      has neither a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tap_root" title="Tap root">
       tap root
      </a>
      nor
      <a href="/wiki/Root_hair" title="Root hair">
       root hairs
      </a>
      , but has a
      <a href="/wiki/Fibrous_root_system" title="Fibrous root system">
       fibrous root system
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pk_14-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-pk-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The coconut palm root system
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
       <a href="#cite_note-15">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        15
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      consists of an abundance of thin roots that grow outward from the plant near the surface. Only a few of the roots penetrate deep into the soil for stability. The type of root system is known as fibrous or adventitious, and is a characteristic of grass species. Other types of large trees produce a single downward-growing tap root with a number of feeder roots growing from it.
     </p>
     <p>
      Coconut palms continue to produce roots from the base of the stem throughout its life. The number of roots produced depends on the age of the tree and the environment, with more than 3,600 roots possible on a tree that's 60 to 70 years old.
     </p>
     <p>
      Roots are usually less than about 3 inches in diameter and uniformly thick from the tree trunk to the root tip.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Inflorescence">
       Inflorescence
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Coconut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Inflorescence">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The palm produces both the female and male
      <a href="/wiki/Flower" title="Flower">
       flowers
      </a>
      on the same
      <a href="/wiki/Inflorescence" title="Inflorescence">
       inflorescence
      </a>
      ; thus, the palm is
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monoecious" title="Monoecious">
       monoecious
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pk_14-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-pk-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Other sources use the term
      <a href="/wiki/Polygamomonoecious" title="Polygamomonoecious">
       polygamomonoecious
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
       <a href="#cite_note-16">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        16
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The female flower is much larger than the male flower. Flowering occurs continuously. Coconut palms are believed to be largely cross-
      <a href="/wiki/Pollination" title="Pollination">
       pollinated
      </a>
      , although some
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Avoid_weasel_words" title="Wikipedia:Avoid weasel words">
         <span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too vague attribution or weasel words. (September 2009)">
          which?
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      dwarf varieties are self-pollinating.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">
       Etymology
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Coconut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Etymology">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Coconut.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Coconut.png/220px-Coconut.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Coconut.png/330px-Coconut.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Coconut.png/440px-Coconut.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Coconut.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A dehusked coconut shell from
        <a href="/wiki/Ivory_Coast" title="Ivory Coast">
         Ivory Coast
        </a>
        showing the face-like markings at the base
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_cut_coconut_shell.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="4608" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/A_cut_coconut_shell.JPG/220px-A_cut_coconut_shell.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/A_cut_coconut_shell.JPG/330px-A_cut_coconut_shell.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/A_cut_coconut_shell.JPG/440px-A_cut_coconut_shell.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A_cut_coconut_shell.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A cut coconut shell
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      One of the earliest mentions of the coconut dates back to the
      <a href="/wiki/One_Thousand_and_One_Nights" title="One Thousand and One Nights">
       One Thousand and One Nights
      </a>
      story of
      <a href="/wiki/Sinbad_the_Sailor" title="Sinbad the Sailor">
       Sinbad the Sailor
      </a>
      ; he is known to have bought and sold coconuts during his fifth voyage.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
       <a href="#cite_note-17">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        17
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       Tenga
      </i>
      , its
      <a href="/wiki/Malayalam" title="Malayalam">
       Malayalam
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Tamil_language" title="Tamil language">
       Tamil
      </a>
      name, was used in the detailed description of coconut found in
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Itinerario" title="Itinerario">
        Itinerario
       </a>
      </i>
      by
      <a href="/wiki/Ludovico_di_Varthema" title="Ludovico di Varthema">
       Ludovico di Varthema
      </a>
      published in 1510 and also in the later
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hortus_Indicus_Malabaricus" title="Hortus Indicus Malabaricus">
        Hortus Indicus Malabaricus
       </a>
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Grimwood1_18-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Grimwood1-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Even earlier, it was called
      <i>
       nux indica
      </i>
      , a name used by
      <a href="/wiki/Marco_Polo" title="Marco Polo">
       Marco Polo
      </a>
      in 1280 while in
      <a href="/wiki/Sumatra" title="Sumatra">
       Sumatra
      </a>
      , taken from the Arabs who called it  
      <i>
       jawz hind
      </i>
      . Both names translate to "Indian nut".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Elzabroek_19-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Elzabroek-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In the earliest description of the coconut palm known, given by
      <a href="/wiki/Cosmas_Indicopleustes" title="Cosmas Indicopleustes">
       Cosmos of Alexandria
      </a>
      in his
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Topographia_Christiana" title="Topographia Christiana">
        Topographia Christiana
       </a>
      </i>
      written about 545 AD, there is a reference to the argell tree and its drupe.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Grimwood1_18-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Grimwood1-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rosengarten_20-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Rosengarten-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Historical evidence favors the European origin of the name "coconut", for no name is similar in any of the languages of India, where the Portuguese first found the fruit; and indeed
      <a href="/wiki/Duarte_Barbosa" title="Duarte Barbosa">
       Barbosa
      </a>
      , Barros, and Garcia, in mentioning the Tamil/Malayalam name
      <i>
       tenga
      </i>
      , and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canarese" title="Canarese">
       Canarese
      </a>
      <i>
       narle
      </i>
      , expressly say, "we call these fruits
      <i>
       quoquos
      </i>
      ", "our people have given it the name of coco", and "that which we call coco, and the Malabars temga".
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/OED" title="OED">
       OED
      </a>
      states: "Portuguese and Spanish authors of the 16th c. agree in identifying the word with Portuguese and Spanish
      <i>
       coco
      </i>
      "grinning face, grin, grimace", also "bugbear, scarecrow", cognate with
      <i>
       cocar
      </i>
      "to grin, make a grimace"; the name being said to refer to the face-like appearance of the base of the shell, with its three holes. According to Losada, the name came from
      <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">
       Portuguese
      </a>
      explorers, the sailors of
      <a href="/wiki/Vasco_da_Gama" title="Vasco da Gama">
       Vasco da Gama
      </a>
      in India, who first brought them to Europe. The coconut shell reminded them of a
      <a href="/wiki/Ghost" title="Ghost">
       ghost
      </a>
      or
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Witch" title="Witch">
       witch
      </a>
      in Portuguese folklore called
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuco" title="Cuco">
        coco
       </a>
      </i>
      (also
      <i>
       cca
      </i>
      ).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
       <a href="#cite_note-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
       <a href="#cite_note-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        22
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The first known recorded usage of the term is 1555.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mw_23-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-mw-23">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        23
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-etym_24-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-etym-24">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        24
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Specific_name_(botany)" title="Specific name (botany)">
       specific name
      </a>
      <i>
       nucifera
      </i>
      is Latin for "nut-bearing".
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Origin.2C_domestication.2C_and_dispersal">
       Origin, domestication, and dispersal
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Coconut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Origin, domestication, and dispersal">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Origin">
       Origin
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Coconut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Origin">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Coconut_distribution.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1187" data-file-width="1910" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Coconut_distribution.png/220px-Coconut_distribution.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Coconut_distribution.png/330px-Coconut_distribution.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Coconut_distribution.png/440px-Coconut_distribution.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Coconut_distribution.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The range of the natural habitat of the coconut palm tree delineated by the red line (based on information in Werth 1933,
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
         <a href="#cite_note-25">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          25
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
        slightly modified by Niklas Jonsson)
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The origin of the plant is the subject of debate.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Grimwood_26-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Grimwood-26">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        26
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Perera_27-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Perera-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jackson_28-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Jackson-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      O.F. Cook was one of the earliest modern researchers to draw conclusions about the location of origin of
      <i>
       Cocos nucifera
      </i>
      based on its current-day worldwide distribution.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cook_29-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Cook-29">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        29
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He hypothesized that the coconut originated in the Americas, based on his belief that American coconut populations predated European contact and because he considered pan-tropical distribution by ocean currents improbable.
      <a href="/wiki/Thor_Heyerdahl" title="Thor Heyerdahl">
       Thor Heyerdahl
      </a>
      later used this hypothesis of the American origin of the coconut to support his theory that the Pacific Islanders originated in South America.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Heyerdahl_30-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Heyerdahl-30">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, more evidence exists for an Indo-Pacific origin either around
      <a href="/wiki/Melanesia" title="Melanesia">
       Melanesia
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Malesia" title="Malesia">
       Malesia
      </a>
      or the
      <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">
       Indian Ocean
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Grimwood_26-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Grimwood-26">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        26
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Perera_27-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Perera-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jackson_28-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Jackson-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The oldest fossils known of the modern coconut dating from the
      <a href="/wiki/Eocene" title="Eocene">
       Eocene
      </a>
      period from around 37 to 55 million years ago were found in Australia and India. However, older palm fossils such as some of
      <a href="/wiki/Nypa_fruticans" title="Nypa fruticans">
       nipa
      </a>
      fruit have been found in the Americas.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jackson_28-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Jackson-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Since 1978, the work on tracing the probable origin and dispersal of
      <i>
       Cocos nucifera
      </i>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Harries_31-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Harries-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      has only recently been augmented by a publication on the germination rate of the coconut seednut
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HCH1_32-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HCH1-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and another on the importance of the coral atoll ecosystem.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HCH_CRC_33-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HCH_CRC-33">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        33
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Briefly, the coconut originated in the coral atoll ecosystem - without human intervention - and required a thick husk and slow germination to survive and disperse.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Domestication">
       Domestication
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Coconut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Domestication">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Coconuts could not reach inland locations without human intervention (to carry seednuts, plant seedlings, etc.) and it was early germination on the palm (vivipary) that was important,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HCH_2_34-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HCH_2-34">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        34
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      rather than increasing the number or size of the edible parts of a fruit that was already large enough. Human cultivation of the coconut selected, not for larger size, but for thinner husks and increased volume of endosperm, the solid meat or liquid water that provides the fruit its food value. Although these modifications for domestication would reduce the fruits ability to float, this ability would be irrelevant to a cultivated population.
     </p>
     <p>
      Among modern C. nucifera, two major types or variants: a thick-husked, angular fruit and a thin-husked, spherical fruit with a higher proportion of endosperm reflect a trend of cultivation in
      <i>
       C. nucifera
      </i>
      : the first coconuts were of the
      <i>
       niu kafa
      </i>
      type, with thick husks to protect the seed, an angular, highly ridged shape to promote buoyancy during ocean dispersal, and a pointed base that allowed fruits to dig into the sand, preventing them from being washed away during germination on a new island. As early human communities began to harvest coconuts for eating and planting, they (perhaps unintentionally) selected for a larger endosperm to husk ratio and a broader, spherical base, which rendered the fruit useful as a cup or bowl, thus creating the
      <i>
       niu vai
      </i>
      type. The decreased buoyancy and increased fragility of this spherical, thin-husked fruit would not matter for a species that had started to be dispersed by humans and grown in plantations. Harries adoption of the Polynesian terms
      <i>
       niu kafa
      </i>
      and
      <i>
       niu vai
      </i>
      has now passed into general scientific discourse, and his hypothesis is generally accepted.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lebrun_35-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Lebrun-35">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        35
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shukla_36-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Shukla-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Variants of
      <i>
       C. nucifera
      </i>
      are also categorized as Tall (var.
      <i>
       typical
      </i>
      ) or Dwarf (var.
      <i>
       nana
      </i>
      ).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Santos_37-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Santos-37">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        37
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The two groups are genetically distinct, with the Dwarf variety showing a greater degree of artificial selection for ornamental traits and for early germination and fruiting.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Harries_31-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Harries-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Huang_38-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Huang-38">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        38
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Tall variety is outcrossing while Dwarf palms are incrossing, which has led to a much greater degree of genetic diversity within the Tall group. It is believed that the Dwarf subgroup mutated from the Tall group under human selection pressure.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rivera_39-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Rivera-39">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        39
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Dispersal">
       Dispersal
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Coconut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Dispersal">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Genomics_of_domestication" title="Genomics of domestication">
       Genomics of domestication
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      It is often cited that coconuts can travel 110 days, or 3,000 miles (4,800km), by sea and still be able to germinate.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Edmondson_40-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Edmondson-40">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        40
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      This figure has been questioned based on the extremely small sample size of the paper that makes this claim.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ward_41-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Ward-41">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        41
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Thor_Heyerdahl" title="Thor Heyerdahl">
       Thor Heyerdahl
      </a>
      provides an alternative, and much shorter, estimate based on his first-hand experience crossing the Pacific Ocean on the raft
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kon-Tiki" title="Kon-Tiki">
       Kon-Tiki
      </a>
      : The nuts we had in baskets on deck remained edible and capable of germinating the whole way to Polynesia. But we had laid about half among the special provisions below deck, with the waves washing around them. Every single one of these was ruined by the sea water. And no coconut can float over the sea faster than a balsa raft moves with the wind behind it."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Heyerdahl_30-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Heyerdahl-30">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He also notes that several of the nuts began to germinate by the time they had been ten weeks at sea, precluding an unassisted journey of 100 days or more. However, it is more than likely that the coconut variety Heyerdahl chose for his long sea voyage was of the large, fleshy, spherical
      <i>
       niu vai
      </i>
      type, which Harries observed to have a significantly shorter germination type and worse buoyancy than the uncultivated
      <i>
       niu kafa
      </i>
      type.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Harries_31-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Harries-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Therefore Heyerdahls observations cannot be considered conclusive when it comes to determining the independent dispersal ability of the uncultivated coconut.
     </p>
     <p>
      Drift models based on wind and ocean currents have shown that coconuts could not have drifted across the Pacific unaided.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ward_41-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Ward-41">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        41
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      This provides some circumstantial evidence that
      <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_peoples" title="Austronesian peoples">
       Austronesian peoples
      </a>
      carried coconuts across the ocean and that they could not have dispersed worldwide without human agency. More recently, genomic analysis of cultivated coconut (
      <i>
       Cocos nucifera L.
      </i>
      ) has shed light on the movements of
      <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_peoples" title="Austronesian peoples">
       Austronesian peoples
      </a>
      . By examining 10 microsatelite loci, researchers found two genetically distinct subpopulations of coconutone originating in the Indian Ocean, the other in the Pacific Ocean. However,
      <a href="/wiki/Genetic_admixture" title="Genetic admixture">
       admixture
      </a>
      , the transfer of genetic material, evidently occurred between the two populations. Given that coconuts are ideally suited for ocean dispersal, individuals from one population possibly could have floated to the other. However, the locations of the admixture events are limited to
      <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">
       Madagascar
      </a>
      and coastal east Africa, and exclude the
      <a href="/wiki/Seychelles" title="Seychelles">
       Seychelles
      </a>
      . This pattern coincides with the known trade routes of Austronesian sailors. Additionally, a genetically distinct subpopulation of coconut on the Pacific coast of Latin America has undergone a genetic bottleneck resulting from a
      <a href="/wiki/Founder_effect" title="Founder effect">
       founder effect
      </a>
      ; however, its ancestral population is the Pacific coconut. This, together with their use of the South American
      <a href="/wiki/Sweet_potato" title="Sweet potato">
       sweet potato
      </a>
      , suggests that Austronesian peoples may have sailed as far east as the Americas.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-coco_42-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-coco-42">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        42
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Distribution">
       Distribution
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Coconut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Distribution">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The coconut has spread across much of the tropics, probably aided in many cases by seafaring people. Coconut fruit in the wild are light, buoyant and highly water resistant, and evolved to disperse significant distances via
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marine_current" title="Marine current">
       marine currents
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Foale_43-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Foale-43">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        43
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Specimens have been collected from the sea as far north as Norway.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
       <a href="#cite_note-44">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        44
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In the
      <a href="/wiki/Hawaiian_Islands" title="Hawaiian Islands">
       Hawaiian Islands
      </a>
      , the coconut is regarded as a
      <a href="/wiki/Polynesia" title="Polynesia">
       Polynesian
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Introduced_species" title="Introduced species">
       introduction
      </a>
      , first brought to the islands by early Polynesian voyagers from their homelands in Oceania.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Elzabroek_19-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Elzabroek-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      They have been found in the Caribbean and the Atlantic coasts of Africa and South America for less than 500 years, but evidence of their presence on the Pacific coast of South America predates
      <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">
       Christopher Columbus
      </a>
      's arrival in the Americas.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Perera_27-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Perera-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      They are now almost ubiquitous between 26N and 26S except for the interiors of Africa and South America.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Natural_habitat">
       Natural habitat
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Coconut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Natural habitat">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Coconut_germinating_on_Black_Sand_Beach,_Island_of_Hawaii.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="1944" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Coconut_germinating_on_Black_Sand_Beach%2C_Island_of_Hawaii.JPG/220px-Coconut_germinating_on_Black_Sand_Beach%2C_Island_of_Hawaii.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Coconut_germinating_on_Black_Sand_Beach%2C_Island_of_Hawaii.JPG/330px-Coconut_germinating_on_Black_Sand_Beach%2C_Island_of_Hawaii.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Coconut_germinating_on_Black_Sand_Beach%2C_Island_of_Hawaii.JPG/440px-Coconut_germinating_on_Black_Sand_Beach%2C_Island_of_Hawaii.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Coconut_germinating_on_Black_Sand_Beach,_Island_of_Hawaii.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Coconut germinating on
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_Sand_Beach" title="Black Sand Beach">
         Black Sand Beach
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Hawaii_(island)" title="Hawaii (island)">
         Island of Hawaii
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The coconut palm thrives on sandy soils and is highly tolerant of
      <a href="/wiki/Salinity" title="Salinity">
       salinity
      </a>
      . It prefers areas with abundant sunlight and regular rainfall (1500mm to 2500mm annually), which makes colonizing shorelines of the tropics relatively straightforward.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sppia_45-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-sppia-45">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        45
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Coconuts also need high
      <a href="/wiki/Humidity" title="Humidity">
       humidity
      </a>
      (7080%+) for optimum growth, which is why they are rarely seen in areas with low humidity, like the southeastern Mediterranean or
      <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">
       Andalusia
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
       Spain
      </a>
      ), even where temperatures are high enough (regularly above 24C or 75.2F). However, they can be found in humid areas with low annual precipitation such as in
      <a href="/wiki/Karachi" title="Karachi">
       Karachi
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">
       Pakistan
      </a>
      , which receives only about 250mm (9.84in) of rainfall per year, but is consistently warm and humid.
     </p>
     <p>
      Coconut palms require warm conditions for successful growth, and are intolerant of cold weather. Some seasonal variation is tolerated, with good growth where mean summer temperatures are between 28 and 37C (82 and 99F), and survival as long as winter temperatures are above 412C (3954F); they will survive brief drops to 0C (32F). Severe frost is usually fatal, although they have been known to recover from temperatures of 4C (25F).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sppia_45-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-sppia-45">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        45
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      They may grow but not fruit properly in areas with insufficient warmth, such as
      <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">
       Bermuda
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      The conditions required for coconut trees to grow without any care are:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       Mean daily temperature above 1213C (53.655.4F) every day of the year
      </li>
      <li>
       Mean annual rainfall above 1,000mm (39.37in)
      </li>
      <li>
       No or very little overhead canopy, since even small trees require direct sun
      </li>
     </ul>
     <p>
      The main limiting factor for most locations which satisfy the rainfall and temperature requirements is canopy growth, except those locations near coastlines, where the sandy soil and salt spray limit the growth of most other trees.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Diseases">
       Diseases
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Coconut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Diseases">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_coconut_palm_diseases" title="List of coconut palm diseases">
       List of coconut palm diseases
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Coconuts are susceptible to the
      <a href="/wiki/Phytoplasma" title="Phytoplasma">
       phytoplasma
      </a>
      disease
      <a href="/wiki/Lethal_yellowing" title="Lethal yellowing">
       lethal yellowing
      </a>
      . One recently selected
      <a href="/wiki/Cultivar" title="Cultivar">
       cultivar
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Maypan_coconut_palm" title="Maypan coconut palm">
       Maypan
      </a>
      , has been bred for resistance to this disease.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Pests">
       Pests
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Coconut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Pests">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The coconut palm is damaged by the
      <a href="/wiki/Larva" title="Larva">
       larvae
      </a>
      of many
      <a href="/wiki/Lepidoptera" title="Lepidoptera">
       Lepidoptera
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Butterfly" title="Butterfly">
       butterfly
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Moth" title="Moth">
       moth
      </a>
      ) species which feed on it, including
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Batrachedra" title="Batrachedra">
        Batrachedra
       </a>
      </i>
      spp.:
      <i>
       B. arenosella
      </i>
      ,
      <i>
       B. atriloqua
      </i>
      (feeds exclusively on
      <i>
       C. nucifera
      </i>
      ),
      <i>
       B. mathesoni
      </i>
      (feeds exclusively on
      <i>
       C. nucifera
      </i>
      ), and
      <i>
       B. nuciferae
      </i>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Brontispa_longissima" title="Brontispa longissima">
        Brontispa longissima
       </a>
      </i>
      (coconut leaf beetle) feeds on young leaves, and damages both
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seedlings" title="Seedlings">
       seedlings
      </a>
      and mature coconut palms. In 2007, the Philippines imposed a
      <a href="/wiki/Quarantine" title="Quarantine">
       quarantine
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Metro_Manila" title="Metro Manila">
       Metro Manila
      </a>
      and 26 provinces to stop the spread of the
      <a href="/wiki/Pest_(organism)" title="Pest (organism)">
       pest
      </a>
      and protect the $800million Philippine coconut industry.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
       <a href="#cite_note-46">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        46
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The fruit may also be damaged by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eriophyid" title="Eriophyid">
       eriophyid
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coconut_mite" title="Coconut mite">
       coconut mites
      </a>
      (
      <i>
       Eriophyes guerreronis
      </i>
      ). This mite infests coconut plantations, and is devastating: it can destroy up to 90% of coconut production. The immature seeds are infested and desapped by larvae staying in the portion covered by the perianth of the immature seed; the seeds then drop off or survive deformed. Spraying with wettable sulfur 0.4% or with
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neem" title="Neem">
       neem
      </a>
      -based pesticides can give some relief, but is cumbersome and labor-intensive.
     </p>
     <p>
      In
      <a href="/wiki/Kerala" title="Kerala">
       Kerala
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">
       India
      </a>
      ), the main coconut pests are the coconut mite, the rhinoceros beetle, the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red_palm_weevil" title="Red palm weevil">
       red palm weevil
      </a>
      and the coconut leaf caterpillar. Research on this topic has as of 2009
      <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
       <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Coconut&amp;action=edit">
        [update]
       </a>
      </sup>
      produced no results, and researchers from the Kerala Agricultural University and the Central Plantation Crop Research Institute, Kasaragode are still searching for a cure. The Krishi Vigyan Kendra, Kannur under
      <a href="/wiki/Kerala_Agricultural_University" title="Kerala Agricultural University">
       Kerala Agricultural University
      </a>
      has developed an innovative extension approach called
      <a href="/wiki/Compact_area_group_approach" title="Compact area group approach">
       compact area group approach
      </a>
      (CAGA) to combat coconut mites.
     </p>
     <h2>

       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">

        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>

         <img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Flag_of_Thailand.svg/23px-Flag_of_Thailand.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Flag_of_Thailand.svg/35px-Flag_of_Thailand.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Flag_of_Thailand.svg/45px-Flag_of_Thailand.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
        </span>
        <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">
         Thailand
        </a>
       </td>
       <td align="right">
        1,010,000
       </td>
       <td align="right">
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td>
        <span class="flagicon">
         <img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="1400" data-file-width="2800" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Flag_of_Malaysia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Malaysia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Flag_of_Malaysia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Malaysia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Flag_of_Malaysia.svg/46px-Flag_of_Malaysia.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
        </span>
        <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">
         Malaysia
        </a>
       </td>
       <td align="right">
        605,000
       </td>
       <td align="right">
        F
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td>
        <span class="flagicon">
         <img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Flag_of_Tanzania.svg/23px-Flag_of_Tanzania.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Flag_of_Tanzania.svg/35px-Flag_of_Tanzania.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Flag_of_Tanzania.svg/45px-Flag_of_Tanzania.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
        </span>
        <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">
         Tanzania
        </a>
       </td>
       <td align="right">
        580,000
       </td>
       <td align="right">
        F
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr style="background:#ccc;">
       <td>
        <span class="flagicon" style="padding-left:25px;">
        </span>
        <b>
         World
        </b>
       </td>
       <td style="text-align:right;">
        <b>
         61,965,165
        </b>
       </td>
       <td style="text-align:right;">
        <b>
         A
        </b>
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td colspan="5">
        <small>
         No symbol = official figure, P = official figure, F = FAO estimate,
         <br/>
         * = Unofficial/Semi-official/mirror data, C = Calculated figure,
         <br/>
         A = Aggregate (may include official, semi-official or estimates);
         <br/>
        </small>
        <p>
         <small>
          Source:
          <a class="external text" href="http://faostat.fao.org/site/567/DesktopDefault.aspx?PageID=567#ancor" rel="nofollow">
           Food And Agriculture Organization of the United Nations:
           <br/>
           Economic And Social Department: The Statistical Division
          </a>
         </small>
        </p>
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <p>
      Coconut palms are grown in more than 90 countries of the world, with a total production of 62million tonnes per year.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
       <a href="#cite_note-47">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        47
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Most of the world production is in tropical Asia. Coconut trees are very hard to establish in dry climates, and cannot grow there without frequent irrigation; in drought conditions, the new leaves do not open well, and older leaves may become desiccated; fruit also tends to be shed.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sppia_45-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-sppia-45">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        45
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The extent of cultivation in the tropics is threatening a number of habitats, such as
      <a href="/wiki/Mangrove" title="Mangrove">
       mangroves
      </a>
      ; an example of such damage to an ecoregion is in the Petenes mangroves of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yucat%C3%A1n_region" title="Yucatn region">
       Yucatn
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
       <a href="#cite_note-48">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        48
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Harvesting">
       Harvesting
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Coconut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Harvesting">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      In some parts of the world (Thailand and Malaysia), trained
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southern_Pig-tailed_Macaque" title="Southern Pig-tailed Macaque">
       pig-tailed macaques
      </a>
      are used to harvest coconuts. Training schools for pig-tailed macaques still exist both in southern
      <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">
       Thailand
      </a>
      and in the
      <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">
       Malaysian
      </a>
      state of
      <a href="/wiki/Kelantan" title="Kelantan">
       Kelantan
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
       <a href="#cite_note-49">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        49
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Competitions are held each year to find the fastest harvester.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="India">
       India
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Coconut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: India">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Coconut_Market.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2707" data-file-width="2521" height="236" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Coconut_Market.JPG/220px-Coconut_Market.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Coconut_Market.JPG/330px-Coconut_Market.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Coconut_Market.JPG/440px-Coconut_Market.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
