        Coconuts being sold on a street in India
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%E0%B4%A4%E0%B5%87%E0%B4%99%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%99%E0%B4%BE_%E0%B4%AA%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%B0%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%BD.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2816" data-file-width="1584" height="320" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/%E0%B4%A4%E0%B5%87%E0%B4%99%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%99%E0%B4%BE_%E0%B4%AA%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%B0%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%BD.jpg/180px-%E0%B4%A4%E0%B5%87%E0%B4%99%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%99%E0%B4%BE_%E0%B4%AA%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%B0%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%BD.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/%E0%B4%A4%E0%B5%87%E0%B4%99%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%99%E0%B4%BE_%E0%B4%AA%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%B0%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%BD.jpg/270px-%E0%B4%A4%E0%B5%87%E0%B4%99%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%99%E0%B4%BE_%E0%B4%AA%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%B0%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%BD.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/%E0%B4%A4%E0%B5%87%E0%B4%99%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%99%E0%B4%BE_%E0%B4%AA%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%B0%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%BD.jpg/360px-%E0%B4%A4%E0%B5%87%E0%B4%99%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%99%E0%B4%BE_%E0%B4%AA%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%B0%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%BD.jpg 2x" width="180"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%E0%B4%A4%E0%B5%87%E0%B4%99%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%99%E0%B4%BE_%E0%B4%AA%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%B0%E0%B4%BF%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%8D%E0%B4%95%E0%B5%BD.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Coconut plucking in Kerala, India
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Maldives_100rufiyaa.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="414" data-file-width="881" height="103" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Maldives_100rufiyaa.jpg/220px-Maldives_100rufiyaa.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Maldives_100rufiyaa.jpg/330px-Maldives_100rufiyaa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Maldives_100rufiyaa.jpg/440px-Maldives_100rufiyaa.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Maldives_100rufiyaa.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Green coconut fruit strands on the tree are featured on each
        <a href="/wiki/Maldivian_rufiyaa" title="Maldivian rufiyaa">
         Maldivian rufiyaa
        </a>
        banknote
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kallar,_Kerala.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3072" data-file-width="4608" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Kallar%2C_Kerala.jpg/220px-Kallar%2C_Kerala.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Kallar%2C_Kerala.jpg/330px-Kallar%2C_Kerala.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Kallar%2C_Kerala.jpg/440px-Kallar%2C_Kerala.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kallar,_Kerala.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Coconut trees are among the most common sights throughout Kerala
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Traditional areas of coconut cultivation in India are the states of
      <a href="/wiki/Kerala" title="Kerala">
       Kerala
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Tamil_Nadu" title="Tamil Nadu">
       Tamil Nadu
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Karnataka" title="Karnataka">
       Karnataka
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Puducherry" title="Puducherry">
       Puducherry
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Andhra_Pradesh" title="Andhra Pradesh">
       Andhra Pradesh
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Goa" title="Goa">
       Goa
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Maharashtra" title="Maharashtra">
       Maharashtra
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Odisha" title="Odisha">
       Odisha
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/West_Bengal" title="West Bengal">
       West Bengal
      </a>
      and the islands of
      <a href="/wiki/Lakshadweep" title="Lakshadweep">
       Lakshadweep
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Andaman_and_Nicobar" title="Andaman and Nicobar">
       Andaman and Nicobar
      </a>
      . Four southern states combined account for almost 92% of the total production in the country: Kerala (45.22%), Tamil Nadu (26.56%), Karnataka (10.85%), and Andhra Pradesh (8.93%).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
       <a href="#cite_note-50">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        50
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Other states, such as Goa, Maharashtra, Odisha, West Bengal, and those in the northeast (
      <a href="/wiki/Tripura" title="Tripura">
       Tripura
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Assam" title="Assam">
       Assam
      </a>
      ) account for the remaining 8.44%. Kerala, which has the largest number of coconut trees, is famous for its coconut-based productscoconut water, copra,
      <a href="/wiki/Coconut_oil" title="Coconut oil">
       coconut oil
      </a>
      , coconut cake (also called coconut meal, copra cake, or copra meal), coconut toddy, coconut shell-based products, coconut wood-based products, coconut leaves, and coir pith.
     </p>
     <p>
      Various terms, such as copra and coir, are derived from the native Malayalam language. In Kerala, the coconut tree is called "Thengu" also termed as
      <i>
       kalpa vriksham
      </i>
      , which essentially means all parts of a coconut tree is useful some way or other.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Maldives">
       Maldives
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Coconut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Maldives">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The coconut is the national tree of the
      <a href="/wiki/Maldives" title="Maldives">
       Maldives
      </a>
      and is considered the most important plant in the country. A coconut tree is also included in the country's national emblem or coat of arms. Coconut trees are grown on all the islands. Before modern construction methods were introduced, coconut leaves were used as roofing material for many houses in the islands, while
      <a href="/wiki/Coconut_timber" title="Coconut timber">
       coconut timber
      </a>
      was used to build houses and boats.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_East">
       Middle East
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Coconut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Middle East">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The main coconut-producing area in the Middle East is the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dhofar" title="Dhofar">
       Dhofar
      </a>
      region of
      <a href="/wiki/Oman" title="Oman">
       Oman
      </a>
      , but they can be grown all along the
      <a href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf" title="Persian Gulf">
       Persian Gulf
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Sea" title="Arabian Sea">
       Arabian Sea
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">
       Red Sea
      </a>
      coasts, because these seas are tropical and provide enough humidity (through seawater evaporation) for coconut trees to grow. The young coconut plants need to be nursed and irrigated with drip pipes until they are old enough (stem bulb development) to be irrigated with brackish water or seawater alone, after which they can be replanted on the beaches. In particular, the area around
      <a href="/wiki/Salalah" title="Salalah">
       Salalah
      </a>
      maintains large coconut plantations similar to those found across the Arabian Sea in Kerala. The reasons why coconut are cultivated only in
      <a href="/wiki/Yemen" title="Yemen">
       Yemen
      </a>
      's
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al_Mahrah" title="Al Mahrah">
       Al Mahrah
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hadramaut" title="Hadramaut">
       Hadramaut
      </a>
      governorates and in the Sultanate of Oman, but not in other suitable areas in the
      <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula" title="Arabian Peninsula">
       Arabian Peninsula
      </a>
      , may originate from the fact that Oman and Hadramaut had long
      <a href="/wiki/Dhow" title="Dhow">
       dhow
      </a>
      trade relations with
      <a href="/wiki/Burma" title="Burma">
       Burma
      </a>
      , Malaysia, Indonesia, East Africa and
      <a href="/wiki/Zanzibar" title="Zanzibar">
       Zanzibar
      </a>
      , as well as southern India and China. Omani people needed the
      <a href="/wiki/Coir" title="Coir">
       coir
      </a>
      rope from the coconut fiber to stitch together their traditional high seas-going dhow vessels in which nails were never used. The 'know how' of coconut cultivation and necessary soil fixation and irrigation may have found its way into Omani, Hadrami and Al-Mahra culture by people who returned from those overseas areas.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Al_hafa_corniche.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="700" data-file-width="1024" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Al_hafa_corniche.jpg/200px-Al_hafa_corniche.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Al_hafa_corniche.jpg/300px-Al_hafa_corniche.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Al_hafa_corniche.jpg/400px-Al_hafa_corniche.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Al_hafa_corniche.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Coconut trees line the beaches and corniches of
        <a href="/wiki/Oman" title="Oman">
         Oman
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The coconut cultivars grown in Oman are generally of the drought-resistant Indian "West Coast tall" (WC Tall) variety. Unlike the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UAE" title="UAE">
       UAE
      </a>
      , which grows mostly non-native dwarf or hybrid coconut cultivars imported from Florida for ornamental purposes, the slender, tall Omani coconut cultivars are relatively well-adapted to the Middle East's hot dry seasons, but need longer to reach maturity. The Middle East's hot, dry climate favors the development of coconut mites, which cause immature seed dropping and may cause brownish-gray discoloration on the coconut's outer green fiber.
     </p>
     <p>
      The ancient coconut groves of Dhofar were mentioned by the medieval Moroccan traveller
      <a href="/wiki/Ibn_Battuta" title="Ibn Battuta">
       Ibn Battuta
      </a>
      in his writings, known as
      <i>
       Al
       <a href="/wiki/Rihla" title="Rihla">
        Rihla
       </a>
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
       <a href="#cite_note-51">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        51
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The annual rainy season known locally as
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Khareef" title="Khareef">
        Khareef
       </a>
      </i>
      or
      <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">
       monsoon
      </a>
      makes coconut cultivation easy on the Arabian east coast.
     </p>
     <p>
      Coconut trees also are increasingly grown for decorative purposes along the coasts of the UAE and Saudi Arabia with the help of irrigation. The UAE has, however, imposed strict laws on mature coconut tree imports from other countries to reduce the spread of
      <a href="/wiki/Pest_(organism)" title="Pest (organism)">
       pests
      </a>
      to other native palm trees, as the mixing of date and coconut trees poses a risk of cross-species palm pests, such as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rhinoceros_beetle" title="Rhinoceros beetle">
       rhinoceros beetles
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red_palm_weevil" title="Red palm weevil">
       red palm weevils
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
       <a href="#cite_note-52">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        52
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The artificial landscaping adopted in Florida may have been the cause for
      <a href="/wiki/Lethal_yellowing" title="Lethal yellowing">
       lethal yellowing
      </a>
      , a viral coconut palm disease that leads to the death of the tree. It is spread by host insects, that thrive on heavy turf grasses. Therefore, heavy turf grass environments (
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beach_resort" title="Beach resort">
       beach resorts
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Golf_course" title="Golf course">
       golf courses
      </a>
      ) also pose a major threat to local coconut trees. Traditionally,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dessert_banana" title="Dessert banana">
       dessert banana
      </a>
      plants and local wild beach flora such as
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Scaevola_taccada" title="Scaevola taccada">
        Scaevola taccada
       </a>
      </i>
      and
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Ipomoea_pes-caprae" title="Ipomoea pes-caprae">
        Ipomoea pes-caprae
       </a>
      </i>
      were used as humidity-supplying green undergrowth for coconut trees, mixed with
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sea_almond" title="Sea almond">
       sea almond
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sea_hibiscus" title="Sea hibiscus">
       sea hibiscus
      </a>
      . Due to growing
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sedentary_life_style" title="Sedentary life style">
       sedentary life styles
      </a>
      and heavy-handed landscaping, there has been a decline in these traditional farming and soil-fixing techniques.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Sri_Lanka">
       Sri Lanka
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Coconut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Sri Lanka">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      An early mention of the planting of coconuts is found in the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Mahavamsa" title="Mahavamsa">
        Mahavamsa
       </a>
      </i>
      during the reign of
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Agrabodhi_II&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Agrabodhi II (page does not exist)">
       Agrabodhi II
      </a>
      around 589 AD.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Grimwood1_18-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Grimwood1-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Coconuts are common in the Sri Lankan diet and the main source of dietary fat.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
       <a href="#cite_note-53">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        53
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">
       United States
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Coconut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: United States">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The only places in the United States where coconut palms can be grown and reproduced outdoors without irrigation are
      <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">
       Hawaii
      </a>
      , southern and central
      <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">
       Florida
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
       <a href="#cite_note-54">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        54
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and the territories of
      <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">
       Puerto Rico
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">
       Guam
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/American_Samoa" title="American Samoa">
       American Samoa
      </a>
      , the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="U.S. Virgin Islands">
       U.S. Virgin Islands
      </a>
      , and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_the_Northern_Mariana_Islands" title="Commonwealth of the Northern Mariana Islands">
       Commonwealth of the Northern Mariana Islands
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Coconut palms will grow from coastal Pinellas County and
      <a href="/wiki/St._Petersburg,_Florida" title="St. Petersburg, Florida">
       St. Petersburg
      </a>
      southwards on Florida's west coast, and
      <a href="/wiki/Melbourne,_Florida" title="Melbourne, Florida">
       Melbourne
      </a>
      southwards on Florida's east coast. The occasional coconut palm is seen north of these areas in favoured
      <a href="/wiki/Microclimate" title="Microclimate">
       microclimates
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Tampa,_Florida" title="Tampa, Florida">
       Tampa
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Clearwater,_Florida" title="Clearwater, Florida">
       Clearwater
      </a>
      , as well as around
      <a href="/wiki/Cape_Canaveral" title="Cape Canaveral">
       Cape Canaveral
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Daytona_Beach" title="Daytona Beach">
       Daytona Beach
      </a>
      on the east coast. They reach fruiting maturity, but can be damaged or killed by the occasional winter freezes in these areas. They may also be grown in favoured microclimates in the
      <a href="/wiki/Rio_Grande_Valley" title="Rio Grande Valley">
       Rio Grande Valley
      </a>
      area of southern
      <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">
       Texas
      </a>
      near
      <a href="/wiki/Brownsville,_Texas" title="Brownsville, Texas">
       Brownsville
      </a>
      , as well as along the upper northeast coast by
      <a href="/wiki/Galveston_Island" title="Galveston Island">
       Galveston Island
      </a>
      , however more severe cold snaps keep them from producing viable fruit. While coconut palms flourish in southern Florida, rare
      <a class="extiw" href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/cold_snap" title="wikt:cold snap">
       cold snaps
      </a>
      can injure coconut palms there, as well. Only the
      <a href="/wiki/Florida_Keys" title="Florida Keys">
       Florida Keys
      </a>
      and the distant southern Atlantic coastlines near Miami provide safe havens from the cold for growing coconut palms on the mainland.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This paragraph provides good information on the tree's range but needs citations (February 2015)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Australia">
       Australia
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Coconut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Australia">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Coconuts are commonly grown around the northern coast of Australia, and in some warmer parts of
      <a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales" title="New South Wales">
       New South Wales
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Bermuda">
       Bermuda
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Coconut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Bermuda">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <table class="metadata plainlinks ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
      <tr>
       <td class="mbox-image">
        <div style="width:52px">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg">
          <img alt="" data-file-height="204" data-file-width="262" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>
         </a>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td class="mbox-text">
        <span class="mbox-text-span">
         This section
         <b>
          does not
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">
           cite
          </a>
          any
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
           references or sources
          </a>
         </b>
         .
         <span class="hide-when-compact">
          Please help improve this section by
          <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing/1">
           adding citations to reliable sources
          </a>
          . Unsourced material may be challenged and
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
           removed
          </a>
          .
         </span>
         <small>
          <i>
           (February 2015)
          </i>
         </small>
        </span>
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <p>
      Most of the tall mature coconut trees found in Bermuda were shipped to the island as seedlings on the decks of ships. In more recent years, the importation of coconuts was prohibited, therefore, a large proportion of the younger trees have been propagated from locally grown coconuts.
     </p>
     <p>
      In the winter months, the growth rate of coconut trees declines due to cooler temperatures and people have commonly attributed this to the reduced yield of coconuts in comparison to tropical regions. However, whilst cooler winter temperatures may be a factor in reducing fruit production, the primary reason for the reduced yield is a lack of water. Bermuda's soil is generally very shallow (1.5 to 3 feet) and much of a coconut tree's root mass is found in the porous limestone underneath the soil. Due to the porosity of the limestone, Bermuda's coconut trees do not generally have a sufficient supply of water with which they are able to support a large number of fruit as rain water quickly drains down through the limestone layer to the water table which is far too deep for a coconut's roots to reach. This typically leads to a reduction in fruit yield (sometimes as little as one or two mature fruits) as well as a reduced milk content inside the coconut that often causes the fruit to be infertile.
     </p>
     <p>
      Conversely, trees growing in close proximity to the sea almost universally yield a much greater volume of fruit as they are able to tap directly into the sea water which permeates the limestone in such areas. Not only do these trees produce a significantly higher yield, but also the fruit itself tends to be far more fertile due to the higher milk content. Trees found growing in Bermuda's marshy inland areas enjoy a similar degree of success as they are also able to tap directly into a constant supply of water.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Cooler_climates">
       Cooler climates
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Coconut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Cooler climates">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      In cooler climates (but not less than
      <a href="/wiki/Hardiness_zone" title="Hardiness zone">
       USDA Zone 9
      </a>
      ), a similar palm, the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queen_palm" title="Queen palm">
       queen palm
      </a>
      (
      <i>
       Syagrus romanzoffiana
      </i>
      ), is used in
      <a href="/wiki/Landscaping" title="Landscaping">
       landscaping
      </a>
      . Its fruits are very similar to the coconut, but much smaller. The queen palm was originally classified in the genus
      <i>
       Cocos
      </i>
      along with the coconut, but was later reclassified in
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Syagrus" title="Syagrus">
        Syagrus
       </a>
      </i>
      . A recently discovered palm,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Beccariophoenix_alfredii" title="Beccariophoenix alfredii">
        Beccariophoenix alfredii
       </a>
      </i>
      from
      <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">
       Madagascar
      </a>
      , is nearly identical to the coconut, more so than the queen palm and can also be grown in slightly cooler climates than the coconut palm. Coconuts can only be grown in temperatures above 18C (64F) and need a daily temperature above 22C (72F) to produce fruit.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Overview_of_uses">
       Overview of uses
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Coconut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Overview of uses">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Coastal_drive_along_KK.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="683" data-file-width="1024" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Coastal_drive_along_KK.jpg/220px-Coastal_drive_along_KK.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Coastal_drive_along_KK.jpg/330px-Coastal_drive_along_KK.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Coastal_drive_along_KK.jpg/440px-Coastal_drive_along_KK.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Coastal_drive_along_KK.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Coconut trees used for landscaping along a coastal road in
        <a href="/wiki/Kota_Kinabalu" title="Kota Kinabalu">
         Kota Kinabalu
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Sabah" title="Sabah">
         Sabah
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">
         Malaysia
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The coconut palm is grown throughout the
      <a href="/wiki/Tropics" title="Tropics">
       tropics
      </a>
      for decoration, as well as for its many culinary and nonculinary uses; virtually every part of the coconut palm can be used by humans in some manner and has significant economic value. Coconuts' versatility is sometimes noted in its naming. In
      <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">
       Sanskrit
      </a>
      , it is
      <i>
       kalpa vriksha
      </i>
      ("the tree which provides all the necessities of life"). In the
      <a href="/wiki/Malay_language" title="Malay language">
       Malay language
      </a>
      , it is
      <i>
       pokok seribu guna
      </i>
      ("the tree of a thousand uses"). In the Philippines, the coconut is commonly called the "
      <a href="/wiki/Tree_of_life" title="Tree of life">
       tree of life
      </a>
      ".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
       <a href="#cite_note-55">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        55
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Culinary_use">
       Culinary use
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Coconut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Culinary use">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Coconut_green.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Coconut_green.JPG/220px-Coconut_green.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Coconut_green.JPG/330px-Coconut_green.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Coconut_green.JPG/440px-Coconut_green.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Coconut_green.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Green coconuts
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Drinking_coconut.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="1944" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Drinking_coconut.jpg/170px-Drinking_coconut.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Drinking_coconut.jpg/255px-Drinking_coconut.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Drinking_coconut.jpg/340px-Drinking_coconut.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Drinking_coconut.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Coconut_water" title="Coconut water">
         Coconut water
        </a>
        drink
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1890_newspaper_advertisement_showing_tin_of_desiccated_cocoanut.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="408" data-file-width="238" height="291" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f4/1890_newspaper_advertisement_showing_tin_of_desiccated_cocoanut.jpg/170px-1890_newspaper_advertisement_showing_tin_of_desiccated_cocoanut.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/f/f4/1890_newspaper_advertisement_showing_tin_of_desiccated_cocoanut.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/f/f4/1890_newspaper_advertisement_showing_tin_of_desiccated_cocoanut.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1890_newspaper_advertisement_showing_tin_of_desiccated_cocoanut.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        1890 newspaper advertisement showing tin of dried coconut
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The various parts of the coconut have a number of culinary uses. The seed provides oil for frying, cooking, and making
      <a href="/wiki/Margarine" title="Margarine">
       margarine
      </a>
      . The white, fleshy part of the seed, the coconut meat, is used fresh or dried in cooking, especially in confections and desserts such as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Macaroons" title="Macaroons">
       macaroons
      </a>
      . Desiccated coconut or coconut milk made from it is frequently added to
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Curries" title="Curries">
       curries
      </a>
      and other savory dishes. Coconut flour has also been developed for use in baking, to combat malnutrition.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
       <a href="#cite_note-56">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        56
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Coconut chips have been sold in the tourist regions of Hawaii and the Caribbean. Coconut butter is often used to describe solidified coconut oil, but has also been adopted as a name by certain specialty products made of coconut milk solids or
      <a href="/wiki/Pur%C3%A9e" title="Pure">
       pured
      </a>
      coconut meat and oil. Dried coconut is also used as the filling for many
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chocolate_bars" title="Chocolate bars">
       chocolate bars
      </a>
      . Some dried coconut is purely coconut but others are manufactured with other ingredients, such as
      <a href="/wiki/Sugar" title="Sugar">
       sugar
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Propylene_glycol" title="Propylene glycol">
       propylene glycol
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Salt" title="Salt">
       salt
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Sodium_metabisulfite" title="Sodium metabisulfite">
       sodium metabisulfite
      </a>
      . Some countries in South East Asia use special coconut mutant called
      <a href="/wiki/Kopyor_coconut" title="Kopyor coconut">
       Kopyor (in Indonesian)
      </a>
      or
      <a href="/wiki/Kopyor_coconut" title="Kopyor coconut">
       macapuno (in Philippines)
      </a>
      as a dessert drinks.
     </p>

      <tr>
       <th scope="row" style="padding-left:0.65em;line-height:1.1em;font-weight:normal;padding-right:0.25em;">
        <a href="/wiki/Monounsaturated_fat" title="Monounsaturated fat">

     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Nutrition">
       Nutrition
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Coconut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Nutrition">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Per 100 gram serving with 354
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Calories" title="Calories">
       calories
      </a>
      , raw coconut meat supplies a high amount of total
      <a href="/wiki/Fat" title="Fat">
       fat
      </a>
      (33 grams), especially
      <a href="/wiki/Saturated_fat" title="Saturated fat">
       saturated fat
      </a>
      (89% of total fat) and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carbohydrates" title="Carbohydrates">
       carbohydrates
      </a>
      (24 grams) (table).
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Micronutrients" title="Micronutrients">
       Micronutrients
      </a>
      in significant content include the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dietary_minerals" title="Dietary minerals">
       dietary minerals
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Manganese" title="Manganese">
       manganese
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Iron" title="Iron">
       iron
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Phosphorus" title="Phosphorus">
       phosphorus
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Zinc" title="Zinc">
       zinc
      </a>
      (table).
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Coconut_water">
       Coconut water
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Coconut&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Coconut water">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Coconut_water" title="Coconut water">
       Coconut water
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Coconut water serves as a suspension for the
      <a href="/wiki/Endosperm" title="Endosperm">
       endosperm
      </a>
      of the coconut during its nuclear phase of development. Later, the endosperm matures and deposits onto the coconut rind during the cellular phase.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-endosperm_6-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-endosperm-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It is consumed throughout the humid tropics, and has been introduced into the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Retail_market" title="Retail market">
       retail market
      </a>
      as a processed
      <a href="/wiki/Sports_drink" title="Sports drink">
       sports drink
      </a>
      . Mature fruits have significantly less liquid than young, immature coconuts, barring spoilage. Coconut water can be fermented to produce
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coconut_vinegar" title="Coconut vinegar">
       coconut vinegar
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Per 100 gram (100 ml) serving, coconut water contains 19
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Calories" title="Calories">
       calories
      </a>
      and no significant content of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Essential_nutrients" title="Essential nutrients">
       essential nutrients
      </a>
      (table).
     </p>

      <span class="mw-headline" id="Coconut_milk">
       Coconut milk
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>

       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">

       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>

      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Coconut_milk" title="Coconut milk">
       Coconut milk
      </a>
     </div>

       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cocomilkjf.JPG">
